If you're lucky enough for it to arrive inprime condition, it's a great deal!

  238. I am a sucker for an eye-shadow palette and I have (I hate to admit it) dropped a couple of hundred dollars at a shot at Sephora. I love Urban Decay and Too Faced and, in budget palettes, Sleek. I am going to be comparing this Shany palette against these other, much more expensive palettes. But first let me say that for the money the Shaney palette is impressive. The shadows perform much better than some other super cheap palettes, like Hard Candy (the Walmart brand) or some of the cheaper drug store brands (e.g. Wet 'n' Wild). The Shany shadows are very smooth to the touch, only slightly powdery, well pigmented, and true to color. Even without a primer, the color lasted me all the way through my Hallowe'en party. The shadows are not, however, as good as UD or Too Faced (not surprising) nor quite as good as the Sleek (the closest competitor with which I am very familiar) or the best of the drug-store brands (e.g. the L'Oreal Infallible eye shadow pans or the Maybelline Tattoo). What are the difference? To my eye, the biggest difference is the quality of the color blend. The Shany are mostly pure single tones. The more expensive palettes are usually a blend of tones. This is especially true of the UD, which have among the best blending of tones that I have found in any shadow products, but it is true for my other, more expensive palettes. I do have one palette with similarly pure tones, the Sleek Ultra Matts V1. Both are very bright, almost \\"neon\\", colors. They both cost about $10. The Sleek palette is only 12 colors, although bigger pans, against the Shany 40. But the Sleek colors are slightly purer, slightly more pigmented, and in texture smoother and less powdery. The two palettes are not perfect substitutes. The Sleek colors are all matte, while the Shany is a mix of matte and relatively subtle shimmer. With 40 shades, Shany palette contains more close shades, making shading and blending together a little easier. Which would I buy if I had only $10 to spend? The Sleek. Am I sorry that I own both? No. In short, if you like to play with eye shadows and your budget is modest, this palette offers a lot of value for a very small price. After trying this palette am I about to go out and buy a bunch more Shany palettes? Not immediately. Will I EVER buy another Shany palette -- almost certainly yes.<br /><br />There were some complaints in older reviews about packing of the palette, so I should say that my palette came inside a box and three layers of bubble wrap and was in perfect condition on arrival.Sleek. Am I sorry that I own both? No. In short, if you like to play with eye shadows and your budget is modest, this palette offers a lot of value for a very small price.   527. Heads up to anyone that purchases this from the seller Makeup & Gift Shop. In the picture, the product is clearly a palette of colors. My photo shows what I actually got.<br /><br />That being said, I'm not going to be one of those ignorant reviewers that leaves one star because I &#34;didn't get what I want.&#34; No, what I got is simply the potted version of the palette (maybe the palette is discontinued?). The quality of the product is impressive. Each color is very pigmented and blendable. My only concern is that, since they are in pots, the application process is really messy. The shadows are a super fine (almost powder) consistency so they love to fall off the brush and get everywhere. Also, the plastic pots the product comes in feels like they will break easily, so be careful not to drop them.<br /><br />Overall, I'm pleased with the product and the color array is awesome. But I wanted to make a review letting others know that you might not get what's in the picture. 4 stars for quality; one star off for being inaccurately portrayed.
